RoboLabs API
OAS 3.0 v2.3.13
Overview Quick start Headers Authentication Rate limits Date and Time External and Internal Identifiers Background mode GET request Endpoints API workflow Versions

RoboLabs REST API

This documentation describes the available endpoints for your database.

A global testing database is available at https://sandbox.robolabs.lt/api/v2.

We recommend using this database for testing and familiarizing yourself with the API. The testing database should not be used to store any valuable or confidential data. Once testing is complete, you can start using the database assigned to your company.

Endpoints API workflow
Base URL: https://jumata.robolabs.lt/api/v2
Content-Type: application/json
Auth: X-API-KEY <API key>

Quick start

1) Get a token in Company profile ? ROBO API ? API Permissions and use it as Authorization: X-API-key <token>.

2) Explore needed endpoints below or jump to the API workflow.

curl -X GET "https://sandbox.robolabs.lt/api/v2/{endpoint}" \
  -H 'Authorization: X-API-key API_KEY'
JavaScript (fetch) 
const res = await fetch('https://sandbox.robolabs.lt/api/v2/{endpoint}', {
  headers: { Authorization: 'X-API-KEY API_KEY' }
});
console.log(await res.json());

Headers

All API requests must include the following headers:

- Content-Type: application/json

- Authorization: X-API-KEY, provide your API key here.

- Language: ACCEPT-LANGUAGE values: en_US, lt_LT (optional, default is provided in the API key settings)

- Execute immediately: EXECUTE_IMMEDIATELY value: true/false (optional, default is false) - if true and background mode is enabled, the request will be executed immediately, otherwise, it will be queued for background mode if it is enabled.

Authentication

To authenticate your API requests, you need to include an API key in the request headers.

You can find your API key in your company settings. The API key should be included in the "Authorization" header as follows:

Authorization: X-API-KEY your_api_key_here

Rate limits

To ensure fair usage and maintain optimal performance for all users, our API enforces rate limits.

The default rate limits are as follows:

- 40 requests per minute.

- 2000 requests per hour.

Some endpoints have specific limits (e.g., sending invoices via email).

If you require higher rate limits, please contact our support team to discuss your needs.

Date and Time

When working with date and time fields in the API, it is important to use the correct format.

All date and time values should be provided in ISO 8601 format (YYYY-MM-DDTHH:MM:SSZ) and should be in Coordinated Universal Time (UTC).

This ensures that the data is accurately interpreted and avoids confusion related to time zones.

External and Internal Identifiers

Each record in our system is assigned a unique internal identifier (ID). This ID is used in the internal processes of the system and ensures uniqueness for each record.

Additionally, each record may have an external identifier (external_id), which can be used to establish a connection between records in our system and your external system.

The external ID is a text that always starts with the symbol "E". For example, "E12345".

Background mode

In the company profile, a manager or accountant can enable threaded API mode, which allows requests to be executed in the background. This mode is particularly useful when you expect a high volume of API jobs or need to avoid blocking the main workflow with long-running operations.

Threaded API mode can be enabled in Company Profile - ROBO API - Enable Threaded API. By default, this option is disabled, but we strongly encourage enabling it if your integration will process many jobs or large data sets. Building your system with background mode in mind ensures scalability and reliability, as requests are queued and processed asynchronously.

When enabled, the API response will return an API job ID instead of the actual data. You can then use the GET "apiJob/id" endpoint to retrieve the results once processing is complete. This approach helps prevent timeouts and improves overall system performance.

{
  "message": "API Call is registered. Passed data will be processed in the meantime. Registered call ID is attached.",
  "job_id": "1"
}
Get API Job Info 
GET /apiJob/{id}

GET request

When executing a GET endpoint, you can control which fields are returned in the response by specifying them in the URL query parameters.

Use the fields parameter and provide a comma-separated list of field names you want to retrieve.

Example:

{endpoint}/{id}?fields=field1,field2

If the fields parameter is not provided, the API will return all available fields by default.
